< review>
They're not the best, but not the worst.  The staff is incredibly helpful, but a majority of their wares are old stock meant to replace very old pieces of household hardware from 30-50 years ago.  They definitely will have screws, bolts, nuts, plumbing, paints, tools, etc, but be careful not to buy a 20-30 year old tool for tree trimming, it will snap.

They honestly need to go through most of their tools stock and mark everything older than 20yrs at 75% off and get some new stock in place.</review>

<response>None</response>< review>
Excellent prices on fresh meat and seafood. The best baked BBQ Pork Baos in Sacramento. Communication is pretty easy when it comes to food,  even with little English being spoken. The staff is old school and quiet so many people mistake this for being rude or conceited but it's really not. The folks there are respectful and kind. If you need help it will come! I've never felt unwelcome or uncomfortable here!

They carry live fish and crustaceans, the pork butt is gorgeous. I made char siu with it and it was better than all the others I've tasted in Sacramento. They have hot foods at nice prices. You can find cookware, frozen Asian convenience foods/snacks like Siu Mai, dumplings, and Baos.

There are sauces/spices/marinades of all kinds, most of which are not carried by major grocers or even advertised and unless you're familiar with Asian foods, you'd be suprised to see them.
They have a small but power packed produce section with real pricing. Fancy stores can sell exotic Asian pears for 4.99 a pound while AFC prices them around 1.99 a pound. The produce always looks fresh and shows that they move what they bring in.

Try the store out and you'll find something life changing!</review>

< review>
**BE AWARE WHEN YOU ORDER COOKED FOOD**

They don't wear gloves when cutting/handling the cooked food such as the roast duck, chicken, pork, etc. When I asked for them to please wear gloves before cutting my duck, the young clerk became very defensive, claiming since her hands were clean the gloves would be unnecessary. However, I saw her using the same rag that she uses to wipe her hands on the chopping board! I then simply asked her not to cut the whole duck and just give it to me whole (since I didn't want someone else's hands on my food before I eat it), and she instantly insulted me, saying "you must not cook at home, huh?" How rude! Why not just put on gloves? Or if you don't have gloves, just tell me, and then not cut my whole duck? This also happened previously when I ordered the steamed chicken, so this definitely isn't a one off thing. That time was worse, though, since they also cut it up right next to the raw chicken and pork. As other people have noted, there are numerous basic health violations. Due to lack of hygiene, definitely don't go here for cooked food. Just go to Ranch 99, it's the same price and at least they wear gloves.< /review>

<review>I've always been wary of pawn shops because I was uneducated and believed the stigma from people who were just as uneducated. I've passed by Traders for years and I finally went in to see about selling an old gold ring I had that I didn't wear.

First off, I was shocked to see how clean and nice it was inside and to see what a big selection of jewelry, tools, music instruments, movies, watches and antiques they had. I was even more surprised to see that it was a family-owned business of some of the nicest people I have ever met. Not only were they nice, there are knowledgeable and extremely helpful.

I also didn't realize that they were a jewelry store with lots of pre-owned, new and custom jewelry. I guess you should never judge a book by it's cover.

I gave them my ring and they appraised it right on the premises, offered me more than I thought I would get, gave me cash and that was it. Totally painless and an actually very pleasant experience.

I'm proud to say that I'm a fan of Traders. Really nice and knowledgable people. Oh yes, and I also felt good about the great security they had. I'm happy I stopped in. I'll definitely be back. Lots of great finds in there too if you're looking for a unique gift for someone or just something for yourself.< /review></record>

<rate>1</rate>< text>
To many vendors not enough people selling stuff they don't want anymore. We like going fleamarkets where people clean out their houses, closets, garages, storage units etc You can find collectibles antiques etc. Why are there so many vendors? If we want to buy new stuff, we know where the store is. This fleamarket is "WAY OVER PRICED" to sell here.  I noticed by just watching, there is more lookers than buyers.  This fleamarket was 100x better back in the 80s because it only cost $7.00 to sell here and it was both parking lots. Hesperian Jack in the box side and also the parking lot near Depot Road. The customers coming to the flea market was complaining so much about no parking and they had to walk so they eliminated the fleamarket on the depo side making it into parking.  So you have one side parking and one side flea market. Customers were still not satisfied because they had to walk back and forth carrying their stuff so Chabot cut the fleamarket in half again making the flemarket half sellers half parking. The time use to be 8 - 4 now it's until 3 pm.  $35 to $45 for 2 parking places? Expensive and not worth it.  $10 should be the price for non vendors and vendors should be little more since they have a business.  I recommend Laney Flemarkey in Oakland off 5th avenue. Yeah they have vendors, they all do, so you cant escape it but I noticed there is lots of old stuff there. Parking is bad I recommend parking at Bart and walk.  Dont know how much it is to sell her but i am thinking it's much cheaper than Chabot and you can see it from the 880 freeway.  They have it every Sunday unless the carnival is there.<//text>

<pictures>None</pictures><rate>1</rate><gmapID>0x809ad638eba5eb45:0x5ea247ce7be8b267< /gmapID><time>1471283899249</time>< Review>
Worst Chipotle I ever visited on 8/06/16, and I've been to many throughout LA. Ordered a quesadilla and it barely had any meat. It was beef which costs the most like $8. Might as well have ordered a burrito and could've actually had enough to eat. Cashier told me I had to cut my quesadilla. How the F am I going to cut it myself? A big floppy piece of food cut on top of foil with a plastic knife? The foil will rip.. It goes through and touches the table, that's not sanitary. Maybe that was a new policy that was recent at that time, not sure, but I've never heard that before from any other Chipotle. I normally never ever complain unless it's that bad. Cashier offered me a little cup of beef that I could add myself to my quesadilla. Talked to the manager about everything and of course she tried to buy me off with free coupons. She looked almost like a kid in high school, didn't seem to know how to handle it. I didn't care about the mishap as much as what was troubling me was all the employees apathetic attitude, no one cared or seemed to desire improvement. If this wasn't a corporate eatery in a busy mall, any restaurant like that would fail miserably. No one wants to pay for horrid service/product. Getting tired of Chipotle in general to be honest, they don't seem to care about customer concerns. I once chipped my tooth on an avocado stem from guacamole and they were supposed to call me back but never did. When there's a new chain that's gmo free, i will switch and never come back. Shameful, really bad business practice. Goto any other location but this one.<//Review>
